05/10/2024, 15:08 - Vedanga: #include <simplecpp>

void checker(char arr[], int first, int last){
    char f = arr[first], l = arr[last];

    if(first >= last){
        cout << "Palindrome" << endl;
        return;
    }

    if (f >= 'A' && f <= 'Z') f |= (1 << 5);
    if (l >= 'A' && l <= 'Z') l |= (1 << 5);

    if(f < 'a' || f > 'z'){
        first++;
        if(l < 'a' || l > 'z'){
            checker(arr, first, --last);
            return;
        }
        checker(arr, first, last);
        return;
    }
    else if(l < 'a' || l > 'z'){
        checker(arr, first, --last);
        return;
    }

    if(f==l) checker(arr, ++first, --last);
    else cout << "Not a Palindrome" << endl;
}

void removeDoubleSpaces(char str[], int& index){
    for(int i=index;i<100;i++) str[i] = str [i+1];
    str[99] = '\0';
    index--;
}

int main(){
    char str[100] = {};
    int t, first, last;

    cin.getline(str, 100);
    for(int i=0;i<100;i++){
        if(str[i] == str[i+1] && str[i] == ' ') removeDoubleSpaces(str, i);
    }

    cin >> t >> first >> last;

    checker(str, first, last);

    for(int i=0;i<100;i++) cout << str[i];    
}

06/10/2024, 20:52 - Parth Bansal: #include <iostream>
using namespace std;
void check_palindrome(char A[], const int a, const int b)
{
    if (int(A[a]) >= 65 && int(A[a]) <= 122 && int(A[b]) >= 65 && int(A[b]) <= 122)
    {
        if ((b - a) == 2)
        {
            if (A[a] == A[b])
            {
                cout << "Palindrome" << endl;
            }
            else
            {
                cout << "Not a Palindrome" << endl;
            }
        }
        else if ((b - a) == 1)
        {
            if (A[a] == A[b])
            {
                cout << "Palindrome" << endl;
            }
            else
            {
                cout << "Not a Palindrome" << endl;
            }
        }
        else if ((b - a) == 0)
        {
            cout << "Palindrome" << endl;
        }
        else if ((b - a) != 2 && (b - a) != 1)
        {
            if (int(A[a]) == int(A[b]) || int(A[a]) == int(A[b]) + 32 || int(A[a]) + 32 == int(A[b]))
                check_palindrome(A, a + 1, b - 1);
            else
            {
                cout << "Not a Palindrome" << endl;
            }
        }
    }
    else
    {
        if (!(int(A[a]) >= 65) || !(int(A[a]) <= 122))
            check_palindrome(A, a + 1, b);
        else if (!(int(A[b]) >= 65) || !(int(A[b]) <= 122))
        {
            check_palindrome(A, a, b - 1);
        }
    }
}
int main()
{
    char arr[100] = {};
    int n, a, b;
    cin.getline(arr, 100);
    cin >> n;
    cin >> a >> b;
    check_palindrome(arr, a, b);
    cout << arr << endl;
}

13/10/2024, 22:15 - Vedanga: #include<iostream>
using namespace std;

int poscomb(int denom[], int n, int target, int z) {
    int ans=0;
    if (target==0) return 1;
    for(int i=0; (target - i*denom[z-1])>=0; i++)
        ans+= poscomb(denom, n, target - i*denom[z-1], z-1);
    return ans;  
}

int main() {
    int n,target;
    cin >> n;
    int arr[n];
    for(int i=0; i<n; i++) {
        cin >> arr[i];
    }
    cin >> target;
    cout << poscomb(arr, n, target, n);
}

27/10/2024, 23:06 - Parth Bansal: #include "myhome.h"
#include <iostream>

using namespace std;

// Constructor for Device class
Device::Device(const string &name, const string &id) : deviceName(name), deviceID(id), status(false) {}

// Turns the device on
void Device::turnOn() {
    status = true;
}

// Turns the device off
void Device::turnOff() {
    status = false;
}

// Returns the device ID
string Device::getDeviceID() const {
    return deviceID;
}

// Returns the device name
string Device::getDeviceName() const {
    return deviceName;
}

// Returns the device status
bool Device::getStatus() const {
    return status;
}

// Prints device information
void Device::printDeviceInfo() const {
    cout << deviceName << endl;
    cout << deviceID << endl;
    cout << (status ? "O" : "F") << endl;
}

// Adds a new device to the smart home
void SmartHome::addDevice(const string &name, const string &id) {
    Device newDevice(name, id);
    devices.push_back(newDevice);
}

// Controls the status of a specific device
int SmartHome::controlDevice(const string &deviceID) {
    for (auto &device : devices) {
        if (device.getDeviceID() == deviceID) {
            if (device.getStatus()) {
                device.turnOff();
            } else {
                device.turnOn();
            }
            return 1;
        }
    }
    return -1;
}

// Lists all devices and their statuses
void SmartHome::listDevices() const {
    for (const auto &device : devices) {
        device.printDeviceInfo();
    }
}

// Lists only the devices that are turned on
void SmartHome::listTurnedOnDevices() const {
    for (const auto &device : devices) {
        if (device.getStatus()) {
            device.printDeviceInfo();
        }
    }
}

27/10/2024, 23:07 - Parth Bansal: #include "myComplex.h"
#include<iomanip>
using namespace std;
// Overload + operator
Complex Complex::operator+(const Complex& other) const {
    return Complex(real + other.real, imaginary + other.imaginary);
}

// Overload - operator
Complex Complex::operator-(const Complex& other) const {
    return Complex(real - other.real, imaginary - other.imaginary);
}

// Overload * operator
Complex Complex::operator*(const Complex& other) const {
    return Complex(real * other.real - imaginary * other.imaginary,
                   real * other.imaginary + imaginary * other.real);
}

// Overload / operator
Complex Complex::operator/(const Complex& other) const {
    double denom = other.real * other.real + other.imaginary * other.imaginary;
    if (denom == 0) {
        throw std::runtime_error("Division by zero");
    }
    return Complex((real * other.real + imaginary * other.imaginary) / denom,
                   (imaginary * other.real - real * other.imaginary) / denom);
}

// Method to display the complex number
void Complex::display() const {
    if (imaginary >= 0) {
        cout << fixed << setprecision(2);
        std::cout << real << " + " << imaginary << "i" << std::endl;
    } else {
        std::cout << fixed << setprecision(2);
        std::cout << real << " - " << -imaginary << "i" << std::endl;
    }
}

#include <iostream>

class Complex {
private:
    double real;      // Real part
    double imaginary; // Imaginary part

public:
    // Constructor to initialize real and imaginary parts
    Complex(double r = 0, double i = 0) : real(r), imaginary(i) {}

    // Overload + operator
    Complex operator+(const Complex& other) const;

    // Overload - operator
    Complex operator-(const Complex& other) const;

    // Overload * operator
    Complex operator*(const Complex& other) const;

    // Overload / operator
    Complex operator/(const Complex& other) const;

    // Method to display the complex number
    void display() const;
};

#endif // MYCOMPLEX_H

27/10/2024, 23:15 - Vedanga: #include <simplecpp>
#include <cmath>
#include <iostream>

using namespace std;

class Shape {
public:
    // Draws an equilateral triangle with side length length
    void draw(int length) {
        for (int i = 0; i < 3; i++) {
            forward(length);
            right(120);
        }
    }

    // Draws a rectangle with length length and breadth breadth
    void draw(int length, int breadth) {
        for (int i = 0; i < 2; i++) {
            forward(length);
            right(90);
            forward(breadth);
            right(90);
        }
    }

    // Draws an isosceles trapezium with base a, top b, and height h
    void draw(int a, int b, int h) {
        double side_length = sqrt(pow((b - a) / 2.0, 2) + pow(h, 2));
        
        forward(a);              // Draw bottom base
        left(120);               
        forward(side_length);     // Draw left side
        left(60);                
        forward(b);               // Draw top base
        left(60);                
        forward(side_length);     // Draw right side
        left(120);                // Return to original direction
    }
};

int main() {
    initCanvas("Shape Drawer", 500, 500);
    Turtle t;
    t.penUp();
    t.moveTo(250, 250);  // Center the turtle
    t.penDown();

    Shape shape;
    char choice;

    while (true) {
        cout << "Enter shape (t for triangle, r for rectangle, z for trapezium, q for quit): ";
        cin >> choice;

        if (choice == 'q') {
            break;  // Exit the loop and end the program
        }

        if (choice == 't') {
            int length;
            cout << "Enter the length of the triangle: ";
            cin >> length;

            shape.draw(length);
            t.penUp();
            t.moveTo(250, 250);  // Return to center
            t.penDown();
        }
        else if (choice == 'r') {
            int length, breadth;
            cout << "Enter the length and breadth of the rectangle: ";
            cin >> length >> breadth;

            shape.draw(length, breadth);
            t.penUp();
            t.moveTo(250, 250);  // Return to center
            t.penDown();
        }
        else if (choice == 'z') {
            int a, b, h;
            cout << "Enter the bottom side length (a), top side length (b), and height (h) of the trapezium: ";
            cin >> a >> b >> h;

            shape.draw(a, b, h);
            t.penUp();
            t.moveTo(250, 250);  // Return to center
            t.penDown();
        }
        else {
            cout << "Invalid choice, please try again." << endl;
        }
    }

    closeCanvas();
    return 0;
}

03/11/2024, 19:03 - Parth Bansal: #include <iostream>
#include "matrix.h"
using namespace std;
#include<vector>
void add(matrix<int>& A, matrix<int>& B, matrix<int>& C)
{
    for(int i=0;i<A.rows();++i)
    {
        for(int j=0;j<A.cols();++j)
            C[i][j] = A[i][j] + B[i][j];
    }
}
void multiply(matrix<int>& A, matrix<int>& B, matrix<int>& C)
{   
    for(int i=0;i<A.rows();++i)
    {
        for(int j=0;j<A.cols();++j)
            C[i][j] = 0;
    }
    for(int i=0;i<A.rows();++i)
    {
        for(int j=0;j<A.cols();++j)
            {
                for(int k=0;k<A.rows();++k)
                    C[i][j] += A[i][k]*B[k][j]; 
            }
    }
}

#include<iostream>
#include<iomanip>
#include <vector>
#include "rental.h"
using namespace std;
Car::Car(string model, string license, float rate)
{
    modelName =model;
    licensePlate =license;
    rentalRate= rate;
}

void Rental::addCar(const Car &car)
{
    cars.push_back(car);
    carCount += 1;
}
void Rental::displayRentalDetails(const Car &car, float totalCost)
{
    cout << "Car Model: " << car.modelName <<endl;
    cout << "License Plate: " << car.licensePlate << endl;
    cout << "Total Rental Cost: $";
    cout << fixed << setprecision(2) << totalCost <<endl;
}
void Rental::rentCar(const string &licensePlate, int numberOfDays)
{
    for(int i=0;i<carCount;++i)
    {
        if(cars[i].licensePlate == licensePlate)
            displayRentalDetails(cars[i],(cars[i].rentalRate)*numberOfDays);
        
    }
}
float Rental::calculateRentalCost(float rentalRate, int numberOfDays)
{
    return rentalRate*numberOfDays;
}

give 2-3 possible ideas of situations, and explain them briefly in a line or two. 

after this, explain the theme you pick in quite detail, and explain ki 5-6 problems will be made by the conveners. the event should be held in som well, its a 
good place to do this. main work of the conveners in this will be to handle all the logistics, make 5-6 problems (and solutions and certain hints), and float
a google form for participating students. realistically, conducting this event shouldn't be too hard bcz a small number of problems will be made and the conveners
will not have to give too much time to this, other than the event day. this event is physics related and is quite interesting because escape rooms is very fun
among young people and should get good participation. purpose: it will add significant value coz this is a super interesting event and participation would be 
quite good, which is the main goal. unique offerings, nothing of the sort is conducted in the club yet. 1 day event, won't really clash with other events and
will add a lot of value to the timeline. event is trendy, bcz escape rooms is quite popular among youth. plan will mainly be:
floating google form, databasing entries, filling incomplete groups, booking som well for the particular day, arranging prizes for winners, refreshments, creating
problems, and other stuff. more rigorous ideation can be done later.

Respected Dean and Associate Dean Sir,

I am Aryan Harshal Puranik (Roll No: 24B2469), writing to bring to your attention concerns regarding the hostel allotment process for freshers for the Autumn Semester 2025 and Spring Semester 2026.

Based on informal information, it appears that an unofficial bidding process was conducted on the night of 23rd and early hours of 24th April, where wings from fresher hostels (Hostel 1, Hostel 16) were allegedly auctioned. Allocations were verbally communicated afterward, leading to widespread confusion and misinformation among students.

Reportedly, wings were sold based on their "quality," judged by participation in sports, cultural activities, and political affiliations. Additionally, political biases seem to have influenced the allocations — wings associated with individuals opposing certain senior hostel authorities allegedly faced discrimination.

Moreover, some students were unexpectedly allotted Hostel 17 and 18, traditionally reserved for senior years, raising further uncertainty about room sharing and allocations for second-year students. Many wings also remain without any confirmed hostel allotment.

I firmly believe this process is unjust. Hostel allocations should be transparent, unbiased, and not influenced by extracurricular or political activities. A few individuals’ actions should not impact an entire wing's future.

I kindly request urgent intervention to investigate this matter and ensure a fair and transparent reallocation process.

Yours sincerely,
Aryan Harshal Puranik

13/05/2025, 23:02 - Vedanga: The objective of this project is to automate core aspects of equity research by leveraging Python-based tools and techniques. Traditional equity research is time-consuming and labor-intensive, often requiring analysts to manually collect, clean, and analyze vast amounts of financial data. This project aims to streamline these processes, enhancing efficiency, consistency, and analytical depth.

The scope of the project includes automated data acquisition from financial APIs (e.g., Alpha Vantage, Yahoo Finance), real-time stock screening based on predefined fundamental and technical indicators, and dynamic report generation using Python libraries such as pandas, numpy, matplotlib, and jinja2. Additionally, natural language processing (NLP) techniques may be used to extract sentiment and insights from earnings call transcripts and news sources.

This automation framework will enable faster decision-making, reduce human error, and allow for scalable coverage across multiple equities. The final deliverable will be a modular and extensible Python application that integrates data collection, analysis, and reporting, ultimately supporting better-informed investment strategies.

\section{End Goals}
\normalsize To gain a foundational understanding of robotics — covering its theoretical and computational aspects — with a focus on robotic arm kinematics, control systems, and simulation. The project aims to:
%The velocity is given by $v = \frac{dx}{dt}$.
\begin{itemize}
    \item Develop a conceptual grounding in the mathematics of robotic motion (forward/inverse kinematics, dynamics).
    \item Gain proficiency in programming robotic behavior using Python and ROS (Robot Operating System).
    \item Explore robotics simulation environments such as Webots to model and test robotic systems virtually.
    \item Build the necessary base to understand and participate in the development or research of advanced robotics in the future.
\end{itemize}

\section{Tentative Deadlines}

\begin{itemize}[itemsep=0.8em]
    \item \textbf{By 17 May 2025:} Review and comprehend the first 10 lectures of the “Robotics” course by Prof. D.K. Pratihar.

    \item \textbf{By 5 June 2025:} Complete all remaining lectures of Prof.\ Pratihar’s “Robotics” course and work through practice exercises from \emph{Introduction to Robotics: Mechanics and Control} (John J.\ Craig).

    \item \textbf{By 14 June 2025:} Finish Python practice on HackerRank and submit the midterm progress report.

    \item \textbf{By 26 June 2025:} Advance ROS proficiency by simulating fundamental systems (e.g., robotic arm, mass–spring–damper).

    \item \textbf{By 10 July 2025:} Develop robot simulations in Webots and submit the end-term project report.
\end{itemize}

\section*{References}

    \href{https://youtube.com/playlist?list=PLbRMhDVUMngcdUbBySzyzcPiFTYWr4rV_&si=UPb7iq_jnU3ynE28}{Robotics – D.\,K.\ Pratihar}.

  \item Morgan Quigley, Brian Gerkey, William D.\ Smart, \emph{Programming Robots with ROS}, O’Reilly Media.

Regarding the video presentation, here are some guidelines : 
- It is advised for you to show your face on video (if only briefly) so that we know that it isn't someone else speaking
- English is the preferred language for the presentation, although, if you really feel you can't speak in English, Hindi is also fine (Please don't use any other regional languages)
- Preferred duration is between 8 to 12 minutes, longer videos are also fine, but as this is intended to cover a small portion of your SoS and not the whole thing, please do not exceed 15 mins.

Some sample videos from previous year : 

1) Abhinav Bijlani (Probability and Statistics) : https://www.youtube.com/live/wuiFkyv053w
2) Aryan Mahajan (Algorithmic Trading) : https://drive.google.com/file/d/1dUTTv0jRZCy-l5wd_CgFWXj_vQNOsyL0/
3) Arnab Choudhury (Quantum Field Theory) : https://drive.google.com/file/d/1drrtPDYqG88vNc0WhX0an0ds1SfNZSzF/

For any queries, please do reach out.

Cheers,
Nirav & Soham
